<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f3a3a84d-95cb-4e52-9f83-4084c02bdfcb'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

As of October 2008, the book has been published in 33 countries around the world, in 30 different languages. A film based on the f</span>
  <span id="freeText3227834758191811935" style="display:none">Vampire Blood Trilogy: The Vampire's Assistant and Other Tales from the Cirque Du Freak, Darren Shan<br />The Saga of Darren Shan (known as Cirque du Freak: The Saga of Darren Shan in the United States) is a young adult 12-part book series written by Darren Shan (pen name of Darren O'Shaughnessy) about the struggle of a boy who has become involved in the world of vampires. As of October 2008, the book has been published in 33 countries around the world, in 30 different languages. A film based on the first three books in the series was released in theatres on October 23, 2009. <br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش:: ششم ماه دسامبر سال 2003 میلادی<br />عنوان: قصه های سرزمین اشباح: مجلد 1 شامل داستانهای سه جلد 1 و 2 و 3: سیرک عجایب، دستیار یک شبح، دخمه خونین؛ نویسنده: دارن شان؛ مترجم: سوده کریمی؛تهران، قدیانی، کتابهای بنفشه، 1382؛ <br />قصه های سرزمین اشباح: مجلد 1 از چهار مجلد؛ شامل داستانهای سه جلد: سیرک عجایب، دستیار یک شبح، دخمه خونین<br />مجموعه کتاب‌های ماجراهای سری سرزمین اشباح: کتاب سیرک عجایب؛ کتاب دستیار یک شبح؛ دخمه خونین؛ کوهستان شبح؛ آزمون های مرگ؛ شاهزاده اشباح؛ شکارچیان غروب؛ همدستان شب؛ قاتلان سحر؛ دریاچه ارواح؛ ارباب سایه ها؛ پسران سرنوشت<br />ا. شربیانی</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Harley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Harley" href="/user/show/70067095-harley">Harley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70067095-harley?shelf=3-and-3-5-stars">3-and-3-5-stars</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2410148758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10419971259014067875"><b>3.5 Stars.</b><br/><br/>This was a fun, nostalgic read however there were a few things I wish I could change about it just to make it that little bit better.<br/><br/>Darren reminded me a lot of Percy Jackson (which was nice, I <i>love</i> and miss him) which gave what was quite a dark, gruesome story a witty edge. Mr Crepsley was for sure my favourite character and I'm excited to read more about him, he's one of those characters that tries really hard to come across emotionless but has a huge heart and it fails them. Despite</span>
  <span id="freeText10419971259014067875" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars.</b><br /><br />This was a fun, nostalgic read however there were a few things I wish I could change about it just to make it that little bit better.<br /><br />Darren reminded me a lot of Percy Jackson (which was nice, I <i>love</i> and miss him) which gave what was quite a dark, gruesome story a witty edge. Mr Crepsley was for sure my favourite character and I'm excited to read more about him, he's one of those characters that tries really hard to come across emotionless but has a huge heart and it fails them. Despite this being a children's book, it didn't read like it. Yes the plot was easy and simple but the darkness was gripping and kept me hooked.<br /><br />My only negative is the use of exclamation marks. They were used at the end of sentences that certainly didn't need them and made the story too immature even though I suppose it would appeal to a younger audience. It's just one of those small things that once I saw it I just <i>couldn't</i> unsee it, although I tried very hard to.<br /><br />I will definitly be reading the next book, I am very curious to see where the story will go.</span>

<div id="review_1329975332" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1329975332" />
    <a title="Annemieke / A Dance with Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17100231-annemieke-a-dance-with-books"><img alt="Annemieke / A Dance with Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563349910p2/17100231.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1329975332?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annemieke / A Dance with Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annemieke / A Dance with Books" href="/user/show/17100231-annemieke-a-dance-with-books">Annemieke / A Dance with Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007306503" href="/book/show/6856011-the-vampire-s-assistant">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17100231-annemieke-a-dance-with-books?shelf=supernatural-paranormal">supernatural-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17100231-annemieke-a-dance-with-books?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17100231-annemieke-a-dance-with-books?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1329975332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13174487449336433797">I watched the movie The Vampire’s Assistant years ago. And honestly, I can’t remember much from it besides the bare bones. However I remember finding the idea interesting and when I found the bind-up of the first three books of the series at Boekenfestijn, I instantly grabbed it. <br/><br/>The overall idea of the world of Cirque Du Freak is solid. It moves away from the stereotypical vampire within mainstream media without losing the essence. That a vampire is a predator. I also mostly enjoy the freak sho</span>
  <span id="freeText13174487449336433797" style="display:none">I watched the movie The Vampire’s Assistant years ago. And honestly, I can’t remember much from it besides the bare bones. However I remember finding the idea interesting and when I found the bind-up of the first three books of the series at Boekenfestijn, I instantly grabbed it. <br /><br />The overall idea of the world of Cirque Du Freak is solid. It moves away from the stereotypical vampire within mainstream media without losing the essence. That a vampire is a predator. I also mostly enjoy the freak show, though sometimes I wished more was done with that. However there are plenty more books in this series. The plot in the first book is a tad wonky, and overall the plot in the first three books do rely heavily in places on not communicating with other people. If some actually talked and were honest, some of the issues would not have occurred. I do appreciate how the author doesn’t shy away from heavier topics, like the funeral at the end of the first book. Plenty of authors would have skipped past that part, especially in middle grade. <br /><br />I have to say that I am glad I got the bind-up and that I read it all right after each other. The books themselves are short. I think they are ideal for the target group, middle grade. I do wish that in the second book the prologue had not been such a summary of the first book and that the first chapter had not been in third point of view. The rest of the book, and the other books, are in first point of view. It didn’t add a whole lot either. <br /><br />The characters are okay. Darren, the main character, I liked initially in the first part of the first book, but with the events in the second half of that book I lost some respect for him because of the decisions he made. However it does show him as a flawed character. Throughout these first three books you do see him grow. This especially shows in the third book. He knows more about being a (half) vampire and doesn’t need to rely as heavily on Mr. Crepsley. <br /><br />I have not decided how I feel about Mr. Crepsley. He’s a bit of a grumpy vampire, and especially in the first book, not all that likeable. I quite enjoy Ezra’s character. He evens out Darren. <br /><br />There are plenty of characters to explore in the next few books, and I can see some possible story lines with them with the hints we’ve been given so far. I think this is an excellent middle grade book for children that love a bit of horror and macabre. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13174487449336433797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText619284088745697672" style="display:none">Superb!! I totally love the first three series of The Darren Shan Saga a.k.a. Vampire Blood. <span id="freeTextContainer14498071955075574593">This teen book about a young English boy who visits the Cirque Du Freak and ends up a vampire's assistant was ok. It was written for teens and should only be read by teens.<br/>The saga of Darren Shan is told in first person. The author does a great job channeling the thoughts, logic, and behavior of a young teen boy. <br/>As an adult reader, it is infuriating but as a pre-teen it is probably perfect and more realistic.<br/><br/>A quick summary: <br/>Darren Shan is a middle school boy. His friend finds a flyer advertisi</span>
  <span id="freeText14498071955075574593" style="display:none">This teen book about a young English boy who visits the Cirque Du Freak and ends up a vampire's assistant was ok. It was written for teens and should only be read by teens.<br />The saga of Darren Shan is told in first person. The author does a great job channeling the thoughts, logic, and behavior of a young teen boy. <br />As an adult reader, it is infuriating but as a pre-teen it is probably perfect and more realistic.<br /><br />A quick summary: <br />Darren Shan is a middle school boy. His friend finds a flyer advertising Cirque Du Freak, an illegal 'freak show'. This show changes everyone's life. His friend recognizes one of the performers as a vampire, begs to be changed to a vampire, is rejected then vows to be a vampire hunter. The next thing you know, Darren becomes a vampire's assistant. The end of part one has Darren leaving town and his friend Steve vowing to follow him to the end of the Earth to kill him. Funny thing--Steve is never, ever mentioned again. So much for that threat. Another thing--why do we need to know that Mr Crepsley went by another name? That is not explained either.<br /><br />Part two is about Darren making a friend. Yeah for him. Darren and his mentor re-join the Cirque so that Darren can have a friend. There is lots of talk of the Little People and Mr. Tiny but no details ever emerge.<br /><br />Part three is about Darren, Evra, and Mr Crepsley traveling to a town, Darren getting a girlfriend, a vampaneze that is terrorizing the town (no one knows it, but he is killing humans).<br />Evra and Darren walk around town a lot--Evra with his scales (snake boy) and Darren in his ridiculous pirate suit--but don't do anything. Then we meet the weird vampanese. The book only gets worse. Of course Darren saves everyone in the end with his quick thinking!<br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer317580249" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14400958207056930281">I read this book some years ago, but it stuck with me in the back of my mind, because it was so unlike anything I've ever read while I was a skinny, too-many-limbs-to-count teen. <br/><br/>The beginning captures your interest, first because it is written in first perspective and secondly because it actually doesn't start with a rainy evening, a clouded day or anything remotely close to what a usual paranormal book starts with - especially when it comes to vampires. <br/><br/>The world is well thought out and it is </span>
  <span id="freeText14400958207056930281" style="display:none">I read this book some years ago, but it stuck with me in the back of my mind, because it was so unlike anything I've ever read while I was a skinny, too-many-limbs-to-count teen. <br /><br />The beginning captures your interest, first because it is written in first perspective and secondly because it actually doesn't start with a rainy evening, a clouded day or anything remotely close to what a usual paranormal book starts with - especially when it comes to vampires. <br /><br />The world is well thought out and it is clear that a lot of attention has been put into the details and in how to make everything come together. <br />The idea of a circus is not one I have come across before and it breathes new life into a world which have slowly been taken over by whimpy vampires with no weaknesses who eats animal blood. <br /><br />But, as you grow older, the books are still good and still an enjoyable read, but you'll probably notice the mistakes more. <br />I haven't read them in a long time, but I probably will soon and then I'll return and edit this review to match my new look on the series. <br /><br /><br />As a side note: <br />At least the vampires don't sparkle. Nor do they eat animal blood. Or anything else. They die from the sun and by getting a stake through the "heart". <br />And by throwing together a new vampire world and having a side story with a circus, Darren Shan have now moved to my <i>independent authors</i> shelf. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14400958207056930281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1867276824860737003">This was a great compilation book of the first three in the Cirque Du Freak series. In these first three books we read about Daren becoming the vampires assistant and leaving his family to go away with the circus.<br/><br/>The main character is Daren, a teenage boy who after going to 'freak circus' steals a vampires spider and gets himself in trouble. That's how it all starts, his best friend gets bitten and Daren makes a deal to become the vampires assistant so that his friend is saved. The second book h</span>
  <span id="freeText1867276824860737003" style="display:none">This was a great compilation book of the first three in the Cirque Du Freak series. In these first three books we read about Daren becoming the vampires assistant and leaving his family to go away with the circus.<br /><br />The main character is Daren, a teenage boy who after going to 'freak circus' steals a vampires spider and gets himself in trouble. That's how it all starts, his best friend gets bitten and Daren makes a deal to become the vampires assistant so that his friend is saved. The second book he makes a friend in one of the town the circus is visiting and while fighting his new urges to drink blood tries his hardest to live a normal teenage life. The third book introduces some new more deadly characters, also vampires but offers Daren a chance to get away from his vampire master if he wants. <br /><br />The secondary characters are mostly the other circus performers who I'm sure we'll read more about in the future. <br /><br />The storyline is superbly original and the authors writing is beyond excellent, it's almost become classical. The pacing is great also and I very much look forward to reading the next books in the series, but I can't at the minute as I've put myself on a buying ban due to lack of space on my shelves. <br /><br />4 stars a great series</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185190812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6227073847197279354">This was a great book. I want to read the next in the series! It took me a while (and when I say a while I mean it, it took me a MONTH to finally start consistently reading it) to get through the first book in this 3 in 1 because I found the main character (Darren) a bit too childish for my liking.<br/>What with the picture of the 17-old guy on the front cover I asumed that Darren's character voice in the story would be more mature and I wasn't thrilled by his juvenile thinking. But as I got to the e</span>
  <span id="freeText6227073847197279354" style="display:none">This was a great book. I want to read the next in the series! It took me a while (and when I say a while I mean it, it took me a MONTH to finally start consistently reading it) to get through the first book in this 3 in 1 because I found the main character (Darren) a bit too childish for my liking.<br />What with the picture of the 17-old guy on the front cover I asumed that Darren's character voice in the story would be more mature and I wasn't thrilled by his juvenile thinking. But as I got to the end of the first book I started to become more familliar and accustomed to Darren and began to like him and realised he's not ALL that childish. He's really quite brave and loyal.<br />One thing that does annoying a lot about this piece of writing is that there are too many exclamation marks! In every single chapter there was a setence that was punctuated with a !, so it lost it's affect.<br />Aside from those two things, this is a pretty good book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6227073847197279354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2215620885" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2215620885" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75019297-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513409098p2/75019297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2215620885?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/75019297-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781435101197" href="/book/show/6016202-cirque-du-freak-three-books-in-one">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2215620885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8932026077960540186">The Cirque Du Freak saga by Darren Shan was absolutely amazing, Cirque Du Freak is a young adult fictional story based on the main character, Darren Shan, a young boy whose entire world is changed by a couple stupid choices. Upon first reading the book, I was definitely intrigued by the introduction of the first book. With passages such as:<br/>"In real life, vacuum cleaners kill spiders. If you cross a busy road without looking, you get whacked by a car. If you fall out of a tree, you break some bon</span>
  <span id="freeText8932026077960540186" style="display:none">The Cirque Du Freak saga by Darren Shan was absolutely amazing, Cirque Du Freak is a young adult fictional story based on the main character, Darren Shan, a young boy whose entire world is changed by a couple stupid choices. Upon first reading the book, I was definitely intrigued by the introduction of the first book. With passages such as:<br />"In real life, vacuum cleaners kill spiders. If you cross a busy road without looking, you get whacked by a car. If you fall out of a tree, you break some bones. Real life's nasty. It's cruel. It doesn't care about heroes and happy endings and the way things should be. In real life, bad things happen. People die. Fights are lost. Evil often wins."<br />On top of this albeit, negative, but intriguing introduction, Darren swears that the events in the book are all completely real. <br />Darren's adventure begins at a freak show, where he observes some amazing and shocking things, such as a spider named, “Madam Octa”. His initial interest in Madam Octa is what leads him to learn of the cold vampire by the name of Mr. Crepsley. <br />Now I know what your thinking, "Vampires? I'm out." Have faith in me. This isn't some trashy Twilight ripoff with a more PG spin. This young adult story was tailored to target a young audience, creating interesting storytelling and even encasing the essence of a little boy, too naive and inexperienced in the ways of the "real world". It is this innocence that keeps the reader captivated and sympathizing the young Darren Shan.<br />Throughout the stories, you get to witness the young boy grow and mature. He slowly starts to become more independent and learns to conquer some of the challenges of being a (half) vampire all on his own, such as making friends. Darren’s best friend, Evra, is a performer of Cirque Du freak and easily my favorite character so far. Mr. Crepsley is definitely a close second though. Evra is a shy young boy with a dark past, though doesn’t make much of an appearance after the third book. <br />This book had many funny and even cringe-worthy moments, but my all time favorite would be when Darren was looking for his fangs in a mirror and Mr. Crepsley caught him. This segment introduced some playful banter and even a kinder side to Mr. Crepsley that the reader hadn’t seen before. However, one part that I would change, would be the part in which Darren drinks blood from his good friend while in public. The scene is overall awkward and although crucial to a later problem, could have been approached much better. <br />I recommend this book to people who are looking for an easy, but fun and interesting read about a newer twist on vampires. This story isn’t like your typical vampire romance novel and even has its own backstory, and fully thought out hierarchy of vampire lore, laws, and much more! This story is charming, and although only a small portion of a twelve part saga series, definitely seems to be worth the read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8932026077960540186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2157927134" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2157927134" />
    <a title="Claire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6505494-claire"><img alt="Claire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385048957p2/6505494.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2157927134?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire" href="/user/show/6505494-claire">Claire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789026119866" href="/book/show/8160767-freakshow-trilogie">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2157927134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3224210216096487222">Just a really short review. <br/><br/>I read these books years ago and now got my hands unto it again. I love these series. The way Darren Shan can write it so good. He can make a single scene pages, chapters long and it will still be intersting. <br/>This particular book series, has a very interesting story with many plot twists. Written by a writer who does not shy away from killing characters. Which I like. I like characters to be vulnerable. Even heroes can't always win, right? They don't. <br/><br/>Don't think that</span>
  <span id="freeText3224210216096487222" style="display:none">Just a really short review. <br /><br />I read these books years ago and now got my hands unto it again. I love these series. The way Darren Shan can write it so good. He can make a single scene pages, chapters long and it will still be intersting. <br />This particular book series, has a very interesting story with many plot twists. Written by a writer who does not shy away from killing characters. Which I like. I like characters to be vulnerable. Even heroes can't always win, right? They don't. <br /><br />Don't think that this series is just for kids. I read them for the first time when I was 18-ish, maybe older and loved them to the bone. I'm a bit older now (26), and still love them. I know, not a huge age difference and no, I am not old. But many people seem to think that these books are for children about the age of 12-13. Well they're not. I bet my brother would also enjoy them and he's 33. Heck, if it was my mother's genre, she would love it. The writing is nice and easy, but still full of adult speech and words your 13 year old will not understand. <br /><br />So go buy the series and love them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3224210216096487222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104871497" />
    <a title="Vani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2242532-vani"><img alt="Vani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1240316036p2/2242532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14250057820495852290">I'm reviewing the whole series here since if you're reading this you're probably trying to decide whether to read the books. As you can see from my rating I recommend them. It's a good fantasy series with a darker side and a very interesting moral dilemma at its heart. I would warn more mature readers that this is obviously a young adult series and the first 2/3 books are written in a young adult's style but I would urge you not to let this put you off the plot and the inticracies within. The en</span>
  <span id="freeText14250057820495852290" style="display:none">I'm reviewing the whole series here since if you're reading this you're probably trying to decide whether to read the books. As you can see from my rating I recommend them. It's a good fantasy series with a darker side and a very interesting moral dilemma at its heart. I would warn more mature readers that this is obviously a young adult series and the first 2/3 books are written in a young adult's style but I would urge you not to let this put you off the plot and the inticracies within. The ending is excellent with twists that I never saw coming, though I first read this story about 10 years ago I never forgot the feeling of surprise and satisfaction when I read the ending, hence me rereading it now. I won't say much more for fear of spoilers though I will also suggest that if you enjoy this series go look up more darren shan novels, I haven't read them all but what I've read was even more maccabre and convoluted as these ones.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2657052489870981185">I never expected to like these books as much as I did, and haven't been this excited over something in a while. I had an idea of the story because I'd seen the movie, but these three books were so much better, and I completely devoured it. The only reason it isn't a 5 star rating is because I thought the first book was a little slow, and it didn't end very well so it didn't feel like the book was complete. There was a <i>lot</i> of exclamations as well but once you get a good way into the first book it</span>
  <span id="freeText2657052489870981185" style="display:none">I never expected to like these books as much as I did, and haven't been this excited over something in a while. I had an idea of the story because I'd seen the movie, but these three books were so much better, and I completely devoured it. The only reason it isn't a 5 star rating is because I thought the first book was a little slow, and it didn't end very well so it didn't feel like the book was complete. There was a <i>lot</i> of exclamations as well but once you get a good way into the first book it's brilliant. More of a middle grade, than a young adult, but it certainly has its dark and upsetting bits <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(when Darren faked his death, said goodbye to his family and had to 'watch' them mourn really got me, and the books were quite descriptive with body parts lost) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and I enjoyed reading them for a first time as an adult. All three books are just quick, easy reads, and I definitely intend to continue with the rest of the series.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3588522193" />
    <a title="Bec" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80862727-bec"><img alt="Bec" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602234003p2/80862727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3588522193?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bec" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bec" href="/user/show/80862727-bec">Bec</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3588522193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer642852762562474990">I hold such a special place in my heart for this series and was the first book series I’d ever read growing up. <br/><br/>Where most people would have read Harry Potter as their first book series, which then triggered their love for reading, for me it was this series. Struggling to read growing up, I found the writing style very easy and I loved the story, and especially the characters.<br/><br/>At the time, I had never heard of such a story and I didn’t know about any tropes or cliches, so every twist and turn was</span>
  <span id="freeText642852762562474990" style="display:none">I hold such a special place in my heart for this series and was the first book series I’d ever read growing up. <br /><br />Where most people would have read Harry Potter as their first book series, which then triggered their love for reading, for me it was this series. Struggling to read growing up, I found the writing style very easy and I loved the story, and especially the characters.<br /><br />At the time, I had never heard of such a story and I didn’t know about any tropes or cliches, so every twist and turn was a complete surprise to me. For years afterwards, I would read this at least once a year because I loved it so much. <br /><br />Even though, I am a little old for the story now, I still like to reminisce on it and read it every now and again. It’s gives me such happy and nostalgic feelings. I definitely recommend this to any young children who want to make a start to reading and are not sure which series to start with.</span>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=great-young-protagonists">great-young-protagonists</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=read-more-than-twice">read-more-than-twice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=read-to-siblings">read-to-siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=on-my-bookshelf">on-my-bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=compulsive-page-turner">compulsive-page-turner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=darren-shan">darren-shan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95679289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10752695727741741714"><b>Addictive, thrilling, action-packed, fast-paced, nostalgic, poignant, sheer awesomeness.</b><br/>It’s very rare to find a kids’ series like this – one where you can still enjoy and look back on fondly after growing out of it. One that you can read for the first time as a teenager or adult and still absolutely love it. One that, from the first page, promises excitement, fun and humor, and plot without lags or pause.<br/><br/>It has been such a long time since I first read this series, but now reading the whole thin</span>
  <span id="freeText10752695727741741714" style="display:none"><b>Addictive, thrilling, action-packed, fast-paced, nostalgic, poignant, sheer awesomeness.</b><br />It’s very rare to find a kids’ series like this – one where you can still enjoy and look back on fondly after growing out of it. One that you can read for the first time as a teenager or adult and still absolutely love it. One that, from the first page, promises excitement, fun and humor, and plot without lags or pause.<br /><br />It has been such a long time since I first read this series, but now reading the whole thing aloud to my little sis I feel like I’m slipping effortlessly back into my old self that first discovered Darren Shan and his <i>Cirque du Freak</i>. It was so easy to get caught up in the story again, even though I knew all its secrets and twists and ends. Because unlike other kids’ series, the Saga of Darren Shan is in no way shallow or devoid of life (even with all the death that is in it); it’s got characters with souls, and a story with heart. It is, in my opinion, the <i>best action-adventure fantasy series for young readers</i>, and easily the best out of anything else Darren Shan has written. His <i>magnum opus</i> you could say.<br /><br />Darren Shan (the character) was an ordinary boy who went to an ordinary school and had an ordinary family and ordinary friends. That (of course) all changed one faithful day when he and his best friend Steve get tickets to the Cirque du Freak and cross paths with Mr. Crepsley, a vampire.<br />Being a vampire story, <i>Cirque du Freak</i> well fulfills its obligations of horror, blood, and tragedy. But it does more than simply shape up a story of a vampire struggling to come to terms with his new life as a blood-sucking monster. Darren Shan, our protagonist and narrator, is a brave and selfless but by all means un-extraordinary little boy who finds himself pitted into a whole other world he is unfamiliar with and which feels frighteningly strange to him; a lone vampire child, surrounded by adults who are centuries older than he is, stronger and faster, who scrutinize him with uncertainty. You can appreciate how this story would appeal to kids, because Darren is only around ten or eleven years old at the start of the series, that age where comfort lies in knowing you have to get up for school in the morning, that your parents will look after you, that you’ve got friends to visit and play soccer with. So besides being a vampire story that would look great as a boy’s anime series like <i>Dragonball Z</i>, it is a growing-up story, too. Lots of themes are explored in this series that would get kids to lapse into a contemplative mood they usually don’t experience watching mindless cartoons on TV – themes of loss and love, life and death, humanity, and the conception of good and evil.<br /><br />Plot-wise, <i>Cirque du Freak</i> gets unbearably predictable in most points – but the shocks you do get well make up for those predictabilities. Even my ten-year-old sister could see a mile off what was going to come to pass in later books after only finishing the first, but it is worth seeing the look of absolute horror and dumbfounded-ness on her face when I read aloud a scene or revelation that completely floors her.<br /><br />And that’s another great thing about this series – it does not try to be anything other than what it is. Maybe it feels like Shan is trying to overdramatize a few scenes here or there, but the fact is that they <i>are</i> dramatic, and emotional. <i>Cirque du Freak</i> does not shy away from death, no matter how unfair, and thus does a better job of getting you that much more close to the characters personally, unlike when you watch a cartoon film where you detach yourself from any immediate danger befalling your favorite characters because you know they can’t die.<br /><br />I’d also like to point out that in <i>Cirque du Freak</i> Darren Shan excels at doing the one thing that is almost impossible to do in a long fantasy series – creating a villain whom you love to hate. While reading <i>Cirque du Freak</i>, your blood <i>boils</i> with hatred for the central villain because of how evil and of how much of an utter asshole he is. This is good, because it means that the villain is doing his job well. Generally people love evil villains because they’re just too cool or funny, or hate villains because of how tirelessly lame they are, rather than because of any evil they’ve done (I, for instance, cannot stand Lord Voldemort, particularly when played by Ralph Fiennes, because he is flat out un-scary and cliché). Although Darren Shan’s arch nemesis may have questionable motives, what matters in the end is what those motives have driven him to do – and what the heroes plan to do to stop him.<br /><br />When I first finished the series, in 2008 I believe (probably does not sound like a long time ago but sure feels like it!), I was decidedly unhappy with the ending. I’ve accepted it since then (although my original rating of one star still stands here on Goodreads – I’d change it, except I’d rather keep the memory of the anger I originally felt XD). I’ve even come to think it’s a very passable ending. And reading the ending scene in the beautiful manga adaptation by Takahiro Arai (who drew almost all the characters exactly how I imagined!) almost made me break down and cry. The books are able to get you right where it hurts, and the illustrations in the manga complement that level of poignancy just right.<br /><br /><i>The Saga of Darren Shan</i> does everything right, and is great for everyone to enjoy. Now all it really needs is some kind of television adaptation (that horrible excuse for a movie doesn’t count). I’d love it if they made an anime based off the manga! I imagine older Darren would sound so hot in Japanese.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10752695727741741714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_155712542" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155712542" />
    <a title="TheBookAddictedGirl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl"><img alt="TheBookAddictedGirl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429733485p2/5009509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155712542?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBookAddictedGirl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBookAddictedGirl" href="/user/show/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl">TheBookAddictedGirl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007306503" href="/book/show/6856011-the-vampire-s-assistant">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Pre-Teens, Particularly 9+</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=british-fiction">british-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=pre-teen">pre-teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155712542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14000855112089113696">3¾ <br/>These three books reminded me of that child-like fear of monsters, a time when the fear is more innocent and almost realistic. I’m not sure what it was about the books, but they just took me back to my first horror novel, that scared me far more than it should have, and haunted my nightmares a little. Of course, these books didn’t scare me witless, but the writing and the story brought the memories back to me.<br/>This is definitely a book for younger readers – young teens or pre-teens, maybe 9 ye</span>
  <span id="freeText14000855112089113696" style="display:none">3¾ <br />These three books reminded me of that child-like fear of monsters, a time when the fear is more innocent and almost realistic. I’m not sure what it was about the books, but they just took me back to my first horror novel, that scared me far more than it should have, and haunted my nightmares a little. Of course, these books didn’t scare me witless, but the writing and the story brought the memories back to me.<br />This is definitely a book for younger readers – young teens or pre-teens, maybe 9 year olds and above – and I can see why for that age group Darren Shan is known as “The Master of Horror”. But even if it was quite far below the level that scares me, I actually enjoyed this book quite a lot. <br />Darren was a mystery to me: I couldn’t figure out his age. I saw the movie before I read the books, and pictured Darren as a sixteen-year-old. But he definitely isn’t in the series. It bugged me. Sometimes he’d seem old – but, then again, not surprising after everything he went through – yet he was young enough to get away with drinking blood from his friend’s knee and act like it was a joke. He also cried a fair bit, and was called “young boy”, yet had a girlfriend at one point. So confusing! Also, he wore a pirate-style outfit, which fitted in at the Cirque, but not so much out in public. Despite the contradictions, I quite liked Darren, he was a good lead boy: smart, resourceful, and brave. But still can’t get the pirate and the annoying age stiff out of my head... it’s bugging me.<br />Evra was my favourite character, I think. Evra’s a snake boy, born to perfectly normal parents, who gave him up, so he’s lived in circus freak shows all his life. He’s got a good sense of humour, and I love his easy-going personality, and his attachment to his snake. Also, he’s a really friendly guy who took Darren under his wing, and became his best friend. I just loved him!<br />Mr Crepsley’s kind of creepy, and very mysterious. Although he’s a little harsh at times, and often very distant, I could tell he cared about Darren. And I loved the way Shan slowly revealed snippets of his past, and of the vampire heritage.<br />Cirque du Freak, the first in the saga, is mainly for setting the scene: nothing particularly terrifying happens in it. It introduces all the characters, and presents the world of Darren Shan to us. Admittedly, this one wasn’t as exciting as the others, and was rather short, but it did set the scene well. Basically, it explains how – and why – Darren (the character, not the author) becomes Mr Crepsley’s Vampire’s Assistant, and how he deals with the consequences. <br />The Vampire’s Assistant starts one or two months after Cirque du Freak, and is about how Darren adjusts to life in his new role at the Cirque. It’s far more exciting, mainly because of all the brilliant Cirque members, including The Wolf Man (a half human, half wolf mix – and the blend of the two blood has driven him insane. I don’t even wanna know how he happened), Cormac Limbs (he can grow all his limbs back at will: cool or what?) and Truska (a woman who can grow a beard with a single thought, and make it retract back in as well). And that is only touching the surface of the group. They’re just brilliant, and a really tight-knit group. And then there are the Little People (teeny, carnivorous people who never speak and are somehow connected to Mr Tiny, whose full name is Mr Des Tiny. Mr Destiny. Can’t be coincidence), who appeared in this book, and made me wonder who – or what – they are. I have no idea. But a good book with laughs in it, along with terror, death and insane eco-warrior. I’m all for saving the environment, but this man was seriously unbalanced. You have to read The Vampire’s Assistant to find out what he did, though.<br />Tunnels of Blood takes place a year or so after The Vampire’s Assistant, and is by far the best. Mr Crepsley needs to leave the cirque for unkown business, and Darren and Evra have gone with him. Crepsley disappears at night, leaving Darren and Evra to do as they please, but when six bodies turn up, drained of blood, the two boys instantly become suspicious of Crepsley and his bizarre habits. Could he be the killer? And if he is, what would they do? Yes, this one was more exciting by far, although it starts off not-so-scary, really picking up the suspense approximately half way through. And Darren gets a girlfriend! Sweet, and very interesting to read about. Yes, the best by far, full of suspense, suspicion, murder, and “Young Murlough”, who made me laugh.<br />Other than the age and questionable fashion sense of Darren, there were a few parts that niggled at me. These were the fact that too many “!”s were used. The other is Shan had little snippets at the end of lots of the chapters. Some made me want to read on to see what happened. Others gave too much away and made me want to scream “I don’t want to know this! I want this to be a surprise! A shock, a twist, build suspense!” But, no. I had to put up with annoying teasers that I really didn’t want to know. Plus, no female leads: so annoying! It was boys boys boys everywhere. Admittidly, they were good characters, but still.<br />The good points outweighed it all, though. The chapters were nice and short, making me want to read on, the writing was simple and flowed, and overall the book was rather addictive. I loved the characters, wanted to live in the Cirque, and really liked the way the vampire heritage slowly unfurled.<br />I'm definately either buying the rest of the series, or getting them out of the library!<br /><br />P.S. If you’ve seen the movie, does anyone know why it’s American, why the characters are all older? It doesn’t make sense!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14000855112089113696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5mvjNYIWUfD1bN1rGbxB0idTyN2hLWYgEJbV4q549DphXEmkwggGy7AMep43JfZ0RzABnV834VIbYZ+xY1wEDQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('M+sQT+8xi9hikbD5acDMaFLGzabb8SQDw8TvgxSdqi203Lrery/c4yfxFwxHWXvOMqUE5iXro3HIM6XQ2blaGg==')})
  }

بیشعوری 26 سال پیش نسبت به شخصیت دونالد ترامپ هشدار می‌دهد و به طور آشکار او را بیشعور می‌خواند. در جایی از کتاب بیشعوری به کتاب مقدس بیشعورهای تاجر به نام «هنر دزدی» اثر «دونالد کرامپ» اشاره می‌شود. که مقصود نویسنده کتاب «هن<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText8920653247440562492\" style=\"display:none\">خاویر کرمنت نویسنده کتاب بیشعوری 26 سال پیش نسبت به شخصیت دونالد ترامپ هشدار می‌دهد و به طور آشکار او را بیشعور می‌خواند. در جایی از کتاب بیشعوری به کتاب مقدس بیشعورهای تاجر به نام «هنر دزدی» اثر «دونالد کرامپ» اشاره می‌شود. که مقصود نویسنده کتاب «هنر معامله» نوشته «دونالد ترامپ»، رئیس جمهور فعلی آمریکا، است.\nدر کتاب می شنویم:\n«کتاب مقدس این نوع بیشعورها (بیشعورهای تاجر) کتابی است به نام هنر دزدی از دونالد کرامپ که می‌نویسد:«راستی و درستی، مهمل و بی‌معنی اند. همیشه مفیدترین راهکارها در تجارت، مدیریت درستکاری عداد و ارقام است. چرا باید برای به‌دست آوردن چیزی به سختی و با صداقت کار کرد وقتی می‌توان آن را به راحتی دزدید؟»\nچاره‌ای هم نیست وقتی یک نفر با کمبود لیاقت و توانایی اصرار داشته باشد که در جلسات، مذاکرات و محاسبات به هر نحوی کارش را پیش ببرد، باید کمبودهایش را با حقه بازی، حرافی و بلوف زدن جبران کند. بیشعورهای گنده‌گو از همینجا پیدا می‌شوند. او هنرنمایی یک گنده‌گو وقتی است که سرنخ کلام از دستش رفته باشد و نداند درباره چی حرف می‌زند. چنین بیشعوری خودش را در برانگیختن دیگران (چرندگویی)، خلاقیت(دزدیدن ایده‌های دیگران)، تعامل (ارعاب دیگران) و مدیریت (سرپوش گذاشتن بر گندکاری‌هایش) خبره نشان می‌دهد.\nکتاب صوتی بیشعوری اثر خاویر کرمنت است. نویسنده ای که بیست سال آزگار با بیشعوری خود، خانواده و اطرافیانش را آزار داد. از دید او تقریبا همه افراد بیشعورند. اگر معتقدید که بهتر است کرمنت درمورد زندگی خودش نظر بدهد باید بگویم بی شعوری یک بیماری است که اغلب افراد مبتلا، از آن بی اطلاع هستند و معمولا در قبال این اتهام می گویند: من بي‌شعور نيستم، تو بیشعوري. بعضي خصوصيات مشترك بیشعورها از اين قرار است: خودپسندي فجيع، نفرت انگيزي بي حد، خيرخواهي متكبرانه، ضميرناخودآگاه غيرقابل نفوذ، كسب قدرت با خوار و ضعيف كردن ديگران، امتنا از صفات اصلي انساني و سوءاستفاده بي رحمانه از آدم های ساده. اگر هنوز هم فکر می کنید که تنها همسایه بی ملاحظه یا مدیر بی احساستان گرفتار بیشعوری هستند پیشنهاد می کنم این کتاب را گوش کنید تا با مثال های ملموس خاویر کرمنت مصداق های بارز بیشعوری را در خود و اطرافتان ببینید.\n\nاین کتاب در سال 1990 در امریکا منتشر شد و محمود فرجامی آن را اولین بار در سال 1390 به زبان فارسی ترجمه نمود. هرچند به دلیل نگرفتن مجوز چاپ آن را به صورت اینترنتی منتشر کرد تا بالاخره در سال 1394 به صورت چاپی در ویترین کتاب فروشی ها قرار گرفت. این کتاب در ایران از همان ابتدا با استقبال فراوانی مواجه شد که البته نثر روان و طنزآلود فرجامی در این محبوبیت بی تأثیر نبوده است.\n\nبیشعوری نوعی اعتیاد است مثل اعتیاد به مواد مخدر یا الکل. فرد معتاد تمایل به تکرار کار خود دارد و این اعتیاد از فرد به جامعه سرایت می کند و محیطی آزاردهنده را به وجود می آورد. بیشعورها چندین دسته اند و ویژگی های مشخصی دارند. آن ها قانون های نانوشته ای دارند، مثلا: تمام قوانين براي اين به وجود آمده‌اند كه نقض شوند، اما فقط تو، حق داري كه آن را زيرپا بگذاري نه ديگران و یا تمام مشكلات را ديگران به وجود آورده‌اند. آن ها بر این باورند که علت اعتراض مهم نيست. مهم خود اعتراض كردن است كه به خاطر آن زندگي مي کنند و همواره معترضند.\n\nکمترین بهره ای که پس از شنیدن کتاب می برید، این است که می توانید بیشعورها را بشناسید و از آن ها دوری کنید اما، شاید آنچه که در این کتاب صوتی شنونده را بیش از یک کتاب طنز و یا بیانگر واقعیت های تلخ اجتماعی با خود همراه می کند نشان دادن روش برخورد با بیشعورها و چگونگی درمان بیشعوری است. خاویر کرمنت انواع و اقسام مثال ها از انسان های بیشعور را با ذکر جزئی ترین رفتارها بیان می کند و چون این فضا قصه های واقعی از زندگی خود و نزدیکانش را به همراه دارد شیرینی دوچندانی به کتاب می بخشد.\n\nهرکسی گفته هیچ بیشعوری در دنیا وجود ندارد، خودش هم بیشعور است. من سه تا بچه بیشعور دارم و هر روز دارم هر چهارتاشان را تحمل می کنم. آخر شوهرم هم بیشعور است.\n- خاویر کرمنت؛ Apart from incidents in Egypt, the novel charts Sinuhe\'s travels in then Egyptian-dominated Syria, in Mitanni, Babylon, Minoan Crete, Mitanni, and among the Hittites.The main character of the novel is named after a character in an ancient Egyptian text commonly known as The Story of Sinuhe. The original story dates to a time long before that of Akhenaten: texts are known from as early as the 12th Dynasty.Much concerned about the historical accuracy of his detailed description of ancient Egyptian life forced the author to carry out considerable research into the subject. The result has been praised not only by readers but also by Egyptologists.Waltari had long been interested in Akhenaten and wrote a play about him which was staged in Helsinki in 1938. <span id="freeTextContainer15691484931648130290">Librarian's note: Also writes books for adults under the name <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7790731.Darren_Dash' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darren Dash</a>. Shan</a> and Darren O'Shaughnessy.<br/><br/>Darren Shan (born July 2, 1972 in London, England) is the pen name of the Irish author Darren O'Shaughnessy, as well as the name of the protagonist of his book series The Saga of Darren Shan, also known as The Cirque Du Freak</span>
  <span id="freeText15691484931648130290" style="display:none">Librarian's note: Also writes books for adults under the name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7790731.Darren_Dash" rel="nofollow noopener">Darren Dash</a>. And in the past he has released books for adults under the names <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1304819.D_B_Shan" rel="nofollow noopener">D.B. Shan</a> and Darren O'Shaughnessy.<br /><br />Darren Shan (born July 2, 1972 in London, England) is the pen name of the Irish author Darren O'Shaughnessy, as well as the name of the protagonist of his book series The Saga of Darren Shan, also known as The Cirque Du Freak Series in the United States. He is the author of the series The Demonata, The Saga of Larten Crepsley, and Zom-B. He has also released the stand-alone novel, The Thin Executioner, and the stand-alone short novels, Koyasan, and Hagurosan. Plus, for adults, he released The City Trilogy (originally under the name of D.B. Shan), and Lady of the Shades.. </span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/159041-the-vampire-s-assistant-and-other-tales-from-the-cirque-du-freak">Quotes from The Vampire&#39;s Ass...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;It’s not fair,” Sam grumbled. “People always say ‘when you’re older’ Where would the world be if Alexander the Great had ‘waited until he was older’? And how about Joan of Arc? If she’d ‘waited until she was older’, the English might have conquered and colonized France. Who decides when someone’s old enough to make decisions for themselves? It should be down to the individual.” He ranted on for a while longer, complaining about adults and the “corrupt, bloody system” and about the time being ripe for a children’s revolution. It was like listening to a crazy politician on television. “If a child wants to open a chocolate factory, let him open one,” Sam stormed. “If he wants to become a jockey, fine. If he wants to be an explorer and set off for strange, cannibal-populated islands, OK!&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
